being re organized , so it s hard to point to specific sub directories . </s>  <s> note that there is an older version floating around that does not support jpeg . </s>  <s> portable software for almost any system if none of the above fits your situation , you can obtain and compile the free jpeg conversion software described in 6b . </s>  <s> you ll also need a viewer program . </s>  <s> if your display is 8 bits or less , any gif viewer will do fine if you have a display with more color capability , try to find a viewer that can read targa or ppm 24 bit image files . </s>  <s> there are numerous commercial jpeg offerings , with more popping up every day . </s>  <s> I recommend that you not spend money on one of these unless you find the available free or shareware software vastly too slow . </s>  <s> in that case , purchase a hardware assisted product . </s>  <s> ask pointed questions about whether the product complies with the final jpeg standard and about whether it can handle the jfif file format many of the earliest commercial releases are not and never will be compatible with anyone else s files . </s>  <s> 6b if you are looking for source code to work with free , portable c code for jpeg compression is available from the independent jpeg group , which I lead . </s>  <s> a package containing our source code , documentation , and some small test files is available from several places . </s>  <s> the official archive site for this source code is ftp.uu.net 137.39 . </s>  <s> 1.9 or 192.48 . </s>  <s> 96.9 . </s>  <s> look under directory graphics jpeg the current release is jpegsrc.v4.tar . </s>  <s> z . </s>  <s> this is a compressed tar file don t forget to retrieve in binary mode . </s>  <s> you can retrieve this file by ftp or uucp . </s>  <s> if you are on a pc and don t know how to cope with . </s>  <s> tar . </s>  <s> z format , you may prefer zip format , which you can find at simtel 20 and mirror sites see note above , file msdos graphics jpegsrc4.zip . </s>  <s> this file will also be available on compuserve , in the graphsupport forum go pics , library 15 , as jpsrc4.zip . </s>  <s> if you have no ftp access , you can retrieve the source from your nearest comp.sources.misc archive version 4 appeared as issues 55 72 of volume 34 . </s>  <s> if you don t know how to retrieve comp.sources.misc postings , see the faq article how to find sources , referred to at the top of section 6 . </s>  <s> the free jpeg code provides conversion between jpeg jfif format and image files in gif , pbmplus ppm pgm , utah rle , and truevision targa file formats . </s>  <s> the core compression and decompression modules can easily be reused in other programs , such as image viewers . </s>  <s> the package is highly portable we have tested it on many machines ranging from pcs to crays . </s>  <s> we have released this software for both noncommercial and commercial use . </s>  <s> companies are welcome to use it as the basis for jpeg related products . </s>  <s> we do not ask a royalty , although we do ask for an acknowledgement in product literature see the readme file in the distribution for details . </s>  <s> we hope to make this software industrial quality although , as with anything that s free , we offer no warranty and accept no liability . </s>  <s> the independent jpeg group is a volunteer organization if you d like to contribute to improving our software , you are welcome to join . </s>  <s> 7 what s all this hoopla about color quantization ? </s>  <s> most people don t have full color 24 bit per pixel display hardware . </s>  <s> typical display hardware stores 8 or fewer bits per pixel , so it can display 256 or fewer distinct colors at a time . </s>  <s> to display a full color image , the computer must map the image into an appropriate set of representative colors . </s>  <s> this process is called color quantization . </s>  <s> this is something of a misnomer , color selection would be a better term . </s>  <s> we re stuck with the standard usage though . </s>  <s> clearly , color quantization is a lossy process . </s>  <s> it turns out that for most images , the details of the color quantization algorithm have much more impact on the final image quality than do any errors introduced by jpeg except at the very lowest jpeg quality settings . </s>  <s> since jpeg is a full color format , converting a color jpeg image for display on 8 bit or less hardware requires color quantization . </s>  <s> this is true for all color jpegs even if you feed a 256 or less color gif into jpeg , what comes out of the decompressor is not 256 colors , but thousands of colors . </s>  <s> this happens because jpeg s lossiness affects each pixel a little differently , so two pixels that started with identical colors will probably come out with slightly different colors . </s>  <s> each original color gets smeared into a group of nearby colors . </s>  <s> therefore quantization is always required to display a color jpeg on a colormapped display , regardless of the image source . </s>  <s> the only way to avoid quantization is to ask for gray scale output . </s>  <s> incidentally , because of this effect it s nearly meaningless to talk about the number of colors used by a jpeg image . </s>  <s> even if you attempted to count the number of distinct pixel values , different jpeg decoders would give you different results because of roundoff error differences . </s>  <s> I occasionally see posted images described as 256 color jpeg . </s>  <s> this tells me that the poster a hasn t read this faq and b probably converted the jpeg from a gif . </s>  <s> jpegs can be classified as color or gray scale just like photographs , but number of colors just isn t a useful concept for jpeg . </s>  <s> on the other hand , a gif image by definition has already been quantized to 256 or fewer colors . </s>  <s> a gif does have a definite number of colors in its palette , and the format doesn t allow more than 256 palette entries . </s>  <s> for purposes of usenet picture distribution , gif has the advantage that the sender precomputes the color quantization , so recipients don t have to . </s>  <s> this is also the disadvantage of gif you re stuck with the sender s quantization . </s>  <s> if the sender quantized to a different number of colors than what you can display , you have to re quantize , resulting in much poorer image quality than if you had quantized once from a full color image . </s>  <s> furthermore , if the sender didn t use a high quality color quantization algorithm , you re out of luck . </s>  <s> for this reason , jpeg offers the promise of significantly better image quality for all users whose machines don t match the sender s display hardware . </s>  <s> jpeg s full color image can be quantized to precisely match the user s display hardware . </s>  <s> furthermore , you will be able to take advantage of future improvements in quantization algorithms there is a lot of active research in this area , or purchase better display hardware , to get a better view of jpeg images you already have . </s>  <s> with a gif , you re stuck forevermore with what was sent . </s>  <s> it s also worth mentioning that many gif viewing programs include rather shoddy quantization routines . </s>  <s> if you view a 256 color gif on a 16 color ega display , for example , you are probably getting a much worse image than you need to . </s>  <s> this is partly an inevitable consequence of doing two color quantizations one to create the gif , one to display it , but often it s also due to sloppiness . </s>  <s> jpeg conversion programs will be forced to use high quality quantizers in order to get acceptable results at all , and in normal use they will quantize directly to the number of colors to be displayed . </s>  <s> thus , jpeg is likely to provide better results than the average gif program for low color resolution displays as well as high resolution ones ! </s>  <s> finally , an ever growing number of people have better than 8 bit display hardware already 15 bit hi color pc displays , true 24 bit displays on workstations and macintoshes , etc . </s>  <s> for these people , gif is already obsolete , as it cannot represent an image to the full capabilities of their display . </s>  <s> jpeg images can drive these displays much more effectively . </s>  <s> thus , jpeg is an all around better choice than gif for representing images in a machine independent fashion . </s>  <s> 8 how does jpeg work ? </s>  <s> the buzz words to know are chrominance subsampling , discrete cosine transforms , coefficient quantization , and huffman or arithmetic entropy coding . </s>  <s> this article s long enough already , so I m not going to say more than that here . </s>  <s> for technical information , see the comp.compression faq . </s>  <s> this is available from the news.answers archive at rtfm.mit.edu , in files pub usenet news.answers compression faq part 1 3 . </s>  <s> if you need help in using the news.answers archive , see the top of this article . </s>  <s> 9 what about lossless jpeg ? </s>  <s> there s a great deal of confusion on this subject . </s>  <s> the jpeg committee did define a truly lossless compression algorithm , I . </s>  <s> e . </s>  <s> , one that guarantees the final output is bit for bit identical to the original input . </s>  <s> however , this lossless mode has almost nothing in common with the regular , lossy jpeg algorithm , and it offers much less compression . </s>  <s> at present , very few implementations of lossless jpeg exist , and all of them are commercial . </s>  <s> saying q 100 to the free jpeg software does not get you a lossless image . </s>  <s> what it does get rid of is deliberate information loss in the coefficient quantization step . </s>  <s> there is still a good deal of information loss in the color subsampling step . </s>  <s> with the v4 free jpeg code , you can also say sample 1x1 to turn off subsampling . </s>  <s> keep in mind that many commercial jpeg implementations cannot cope with the resulting file . </s>  <s> even with both quantization and subsampling turned off , the regular jpeg algorithm is not lossless , because it is subject to roundoff errors in various calculations . </s>  <s> the maximum error is a few counts in any one pixel value it s highly unlikely that this could be perceived by the human eye , but it might be a concern if you are doing machine processing of an image . </s>  <s> at this minimum loss setting , regular jpeg produces files that are perhaps half the size of an uncompressed 24 bit per pixel image . </s>  <s> true lossless jpeg provides roughly the same amount of compression , but it guarantees bit for bit accuracy . </s>  <s> if you have an application requiring lossless storage of images with less than 6 bits per pixel per color component , you may want to look into the jbig bilevel image compression standard . </s>  <s> this performs better than jpeg lossless on such images . </s>  <s> jpeg lossless is superior to jbig on images with 6 or more bits per pixel furthermore , jpeg is public domain at least with a huffman back end , while the jbig techniques are heavily covered by patents . </s>  <s> 10 why all the argument about file formats ? </s>  <s> strictly speaking , jpeg refers only to a family of compression algorithms it does not refer to a specific image file format . </s>  <s> the jpeg committee was prevented from defining a file format by turf wars within the international standards organizations . </s>  <s> since we can t actually exchange images with anyone else unless we agree on a common file format , this leaves us with a problem . </s>  <s> in the absence of official standards , a number of jpeg program writers have just gone off to do their own thing , and as a result their programs aren t compatible with anybody else s . </s>  <s> the closest thing we have to a de facto standard jpeg format is some work that s been coordinated by people at c cube microsystems . </s>  <s> they have defined two jpeg based file formats jfif jpeg file interchange format , a low end format that transports pixels and not much else . </s>  <s> tiff jpeg , aka tiff 6.0 , an extension of the aldus tiff format . </s>  <s> tiff is a high end format that will let you record just about everything you ever wanted to know about an image , and a lot more besides . </s>  <s> tiff is a lot more complex than jfif , and may well prove less transportable , because different vendors have historically implemented slightly different and incompatible subsets of tiff . </s>  <s> it s not likely that adding jpeg to the mix will do anything to improve this situation . </s>  <s> both of these formats were developed with input from all the major vendors of jpeg related products it s reasonably likely that future commercial products will adhere to one or both standards . </s>  <s> I believe that usenet should adopt jfif as the replacement for gif in picture postings . </s>  <s> jfif is simpler than tiff and is available now the tiff 6.0 spec has only recently been officially adopted , and it is still unusably vague on some crucial details . </s>  <s> even when tiff jpeg is well defined , the jfif format is likely to be a widely supported lowest common denominator tiff jpeg files may never be as transportable . </s>  <s> a particular case that people may be interested in is apple s quicktime software for the macintosh . </s>  <s> quicktime uses a jfif compatible format wrapped inside the mac specific pict structure . </s>  <s> conversion between jfif and quicktime jpeg is pretty straightforward , and several mac programs are available to do it see mac portion of section 6a . </s>  <s> if you have an editor that handles binary files , you can strip a quicktime jpeg pict down to jfif by hand see section 11 for details . </s>  <s> another particular case is handmade software s programs gif 2jpg jpg 2gif and image alchemy . </s>  <s> these programs are capable of reading and writing jfif format . </s>  <s> by default , though , they write a proprietary format developed by hsi . </s>  <s> this format is not readable by any non hsi programs and should not be used for usenet postings . </s>  <s> use the j switch to get jfif output . </s>  <s> this applies to old versions of these programs the current releases emit jfif format by default . </s>  <s> you still should be careful not to post hsi format files , unless you want to get flamed by people on non pc platforms . </s>  <s> 11 how do I recognize which file format I have , and what do I do about it ? </s>  <s> if you have an alleged jpeg file that your software won t read , it s likely to be hsi format or some other proprietary jpeg based format . </s>  <s> you can tell what you have by inspecting the first few bytes of the file 1 . </s>  <s> a jfif standard file will start with the characters hex ff d8 ff e0 , followed by two variable bytes often hex 00 10 , followed by jfif . </s>  <s> 2 . </s>  <s> if you see ff d8 at the start , but not the rest of it , you may have a raw jpeg file . </s>  <s> this is probably decodable as is by jfif software it s worth a try , anyway . </s>  <s> 3 . </s>  <s> hsi files start with hsi 1 . </s>  <s> you re out of luck unless you have hsi software . </s>  <s> portions of the file may look like plain jpeg data , but they won t decompress properly with non hsi programs . </s>  <s> 4 . </s>  <s> a macintosh pict file , if jpeg compressed , will have a couple hundred bytes of header followed by a jfif header scan for jfif . </s>  <s> strip off everything before the ff d8 and you should be able to read it . </s>  <s> 5 . </s>  <s> anything else it s a proprietary format , or not jpeg at all . </s>  <s> if you are lucky , the file may consist of a header and a raw jpeg data stream . </s>  <s> if you can identify the start of the jpeg data stream look for ff d8 , try stripping off everything before that . </s>  <s> in uuencoded usenet postings , the characteristic jfif pattern is begin line m cx ... whereas uuencoded hsi files will start with begin line m I ... if you learn to check for the former , you can save yourself the trouble of downloading non jfif files . </s>  <s> 12 what about arithmetic coding ? </s>  <s> the jpeg spec defines two different back end modules for the final output of compressed data either huffman coding or arithmetic coding is allowed . </s>  <s> the choice has no impact on image quality , but arithmetic coding usually produces a smaller compressed file . </s>  <s> on typical images , arithmetic coding produces a file 5 or 10 percent smaller than huffman coding . </s>  <s> all the file size numbers previously cited are for huffman coding . </s>  <s> unfortunately , the particular variant of arithmetic coding specified by the jpeg standard is subject to patents owned by ibm , at t , and mitsubishi . </s>  <s> thus you cannot legally use arithmetic coding unless you obtain licenses from these companies . </s>  <s> the fair use doctrine allows people to implement and test the algorithm , but actually storing any images with it is dubious at best . </s>  <s> at least in the short run , I recommend that people not worry about arithmetic coding the space savings isn t great enough to justify the potential legal hassles . </s>  <s> in particular , arithmetic coding should not be used for any images to be exchanged on usenet . </s>  <s> there is some small chance that the legal situation may change in the future . </s>  <s> stay tuned for further details . </s>  <s> 13 does loss accumulate with repeated compression decompression ? </s>  <s> it would be nice if , having compressed an image with jpeg , you could decompress it , manipulate it crop off a border , say , and recompress it without any further image degradation beyond what you lost initially . </s>  <s> unfortunately this is not the case . </s>  <s> in general , recompressing an altered image loses more information , though usually not as much as was lost the first time around . </s>  <s> the next best thing would be that if you decompress an image and recompress it without changing it then there is no further loss , I . </s>  <s> e . </s>  <s> , you get an identical jpeg file . </s>  <s> even this is not true at least , not with the current free jpeg software . </s>  <s> it s essentially a problem of accumulation of roundoff error . </s>  <s> if you repeatedly compress and decompress , the image will eventually degrade to where you can see visible changes from the first generation output . </s>  <s> it usually takes many such cycles to get visible change . </s>  <s> one of the things on our to do list is to see if accumulation of error can be avoided or limited , but I am not optimistic about it . </s>  <s> in any case , the most that could possibly be guaranteed would be that compressing the unmodified full color output of djpeg , at the original quality setting , would introduce no further loss . </s>  <s> even such simple changes as cropping off a border could cause further roundoff error degradation . </s>  <s> if you re wondering why , it s because the pixel block boundaries move . </s>  <s> if you cropped off only multiples of 16 pixels , you might be safe , but that s a mighty limited capability ! </s>  <s> the bottom line is that jpeg is a useful format for archival storage and transmission of images , but you don t want to use it as an intermediate format for sequences of image manipulation steps . </s>  <s> use a lossless format ppm , rle , tiff , etc while working on the image , then jpeg it when you are ready to file it away . </s>  <s> aside from avoiding degradation , you will save a lot of compression decompression time this way . </s>  <s> 14 what are some rules of thumb for converting gif images to jpeg ? </s>  <s> as stated earlier , you will lose some amount of image information if you convert an existing gif image to jpeg . </s>  <s> if you can obtain the original full color data the gif was made from , it s far better to make a jpeg from that . </s>  <s> but if you need to save space and have only the gif to work from , here are some suggestions for getting maximum space savings with minimum loss of quality . </s>  <s> the first rule when converting a gif library is to look at each jpeg , to make sure you are happy with it , before throwing away the corresponding gif that will give you a chance to re do the conversion with a higher quality setting if necessary . </s>  <s> some gifs may be better left as gifs , as explained in section 3 in particular , cartoon type gifs with sixteen or fewer colors don t convert well . </s>  <s> you may find that a jpeg file of reasonable quality will be larger than the gif . </s>  <s> so check the sizes too . </s>  <s> experience to date suggests that large , high visual quality gifs are the best candidates for conversion to jpeg . </s>  <s> they chew up the most storage so offer the most potential savings , and they convert to jpeg with least degradation . </s>  <s> don t waste your time converting any gif much under 100 kbytes . </s>  <s> also , don t expect jpeg files converted from gifs to be as small as those created directly from full color originals . </s>  <s> to maintain image quality you may have to let the converted files be as much as twice as big as straight through jpeg files would be I . </s>  <s> e . </s>  <s> , shoot for 1 2 or 1 3 rd the size of the gif file , not 1 4 th as suggested in earlier comparisons . </s>  <s> many people have developed an odd habit of putting a large constant color border around a gif image . </s>  <s> while useless , this was nearly free in terms of storage cost in gif files . </s>  <s> it is not free in jpeg files , and the sharp border boundary can create visible artifacts ghost edges . </s>  <s> do yourself a favor and crop off any border before jpeging . </s>  <s> if you are on an x windows system , xv s manual and automatic cropping functions are a very painless way to do this . </s>  <s> cjpeg s default q setting of 75 is appropriate for full color input , but for gif inputs , q settings of 85 to 95 often seem to be necessary to avoid image degradation . </s>  <s> if you apply smoothing as suggested below , the higher q setting may not be necessary . </s>  <s> color gifs of photographs or complex artwork are usually dithered to fool your eye into seeing more than the 256 colors that gif can actually store . </s>  <s> if you enlarge the image , you will see that adjacent pixels are often of significantly different colors at normal size the eye averages these pixels together to produce the illusion of an intermediate color value . </s>  <s> the trouble with dithering is that , to jpeg , it looks like high spatial frequency color noise and jpeg can t compress noise very well . </s>  <s> the resulting jpeg file is both larger and of lower image quality than what you would have gotten from jpeging the original full color image if you had it . </s>  <s> to get around this , you want to smooth the gif image before compression . </s>  <s> smoothing averages together nearby pixels , thus approximating the color that you thought you saw anyway , and in the process getting rid of the rapid color changes that give jpeg trouble . </s>  <s> appropriate use of smoothing will often let you avoid using a high q factor , thus further reducing the size of the compressed file , while still obtaining a better looking output image than you d get without smoothing . </s>  <s> with the v4 free jpeg software or products based on it , a simple smoothing capability is built in . </s>  <s> try smooth 10 or so when converting gifs . </s>  <s> values of 10 to 25 seem to work well for high quality gifs . </s>  <s> heavy handed dithering may require larger smoothing factors . </s>  <s> if you can see regular fine scale patterns on the gif image even without enlargement , then strong smoothing is definitely called for . </s>  <s> too large a smoothing factor will blur the output image , which you don t want . </s>  <s> if you are an image processing wizard , you can also do smoothing with a separate filtering program , such as pnmconvol from the pbmplus package . </s>  <s> however , cjpeg s built in smoother is a lot faster than pnmconvol ... the upshot of all this is that cjpeg quality 85 smooth 10 is probably a good starting point for converting gifs . </s>  <s> but if you really care about the image , you ll want to check the results and maybe try a few other settings . </s>  <s> for more information about jpeg in general or the free jpeg software in particular , contact the independent jpeg group at . </s>  <s> tom lane organizer , independent jpeg group internet bitnet tgl cs.cmu . </s>  <s> edu carnegie </s>  <s> from rene s . </s>  <s> dutch student subject interviews graphics package hello , I m trying out the c graphics package interviews . </s>  <s> besides the man pages on barreno ps I start my sabbatical 29 may , ask those questions now </s>  <s> from chris lilley subject re help need 24 bits viewer in article , gilles deniaud writes I m looking for a program which is <s> let s say you have a scanned image of a line drawing in this case a boat , but it could be anything . </s>  <s> on the drawing you have a set of reference points whose true x , y positions are known . </s>  <s> now you digitize the drawing manually in this case , using yaron danon s excellent digitize program . </s>  <s> that is , you use a program which converts cursor positions to x , y and saves those values when you click the mouse . </s>  <s> upon digitizing you notice that the reference point values that come out of the digitizing process differ in small but significant ways from the known true values . </s>  <s> this is understandable because the scanned drawing is a reproduction of the original and there are successive sources of distortion such as differential expansion and contraction of paper , errors introduced in the printing process , scanner errors and what have you . </s>  <s> the errors are not uniform over the entire drawing , so global adjustments such as stretching contracting uniformly over x or y , or rotating the whole drawing , are not satisfactory . </s>  <s> so the question is does any kind soul know of an algorithm for removing such distortion ? </s>  <s> in particular , if I have three sets of points reference x , y the known true values distortedreference x , y the same points , with known errors distorteddata x , y other points , with unknown errors what function of reference and distorted could I apply to distorteddata to remove the errors . </s>  <s> I suspect the problem could be solved by treating the distorted reference points as resulting from the projection of a bumpy 3d surface , solving for the surface and then flattening it to remove the errors in the other data points . </s>  <s> any kind and informed soul out there have you considered the apple laserwriter iig . </s>  <s> we use it for all our b w image printing . </s>  <s> from kenneth sloan subject re surface normal orientations in article 1pscti stephen pietrowicz writes ... how do you go about orienting all normals in the same direction , given a set of points , edges and faces ? </s>  <s> look for edge inconsistencies . </s>  <s> consider two vertices , p and q , which are connected by at least one edge . </s>  <s> if p , q is an edge , then q , p should not appear . </s>  <s> if both p , q and q , p appear as edges , then the surface flips when you travel across that edge . </s>  <s> this is bad . </s>  <s> assuming warning ... warning ... warning that you have an otherwise acceptable surface you can pick an edge , any edge , and traverse the surface enforcing consistency with that edge . </s>  <s> 0 pick an edge p , q , and mark it as ok 1 for each face , f , containing this edge if more than 2 , oops make sure that all edges in f are consistent I . </s>  <s> e . </s>  <s> , the face should be p , q , q , r , r , s , s , t , t , p . </s>  <s> flip those which are wrong . </s>  <s> mark all of the edges in f as ok , and add them to a queue check for duplicates , and especially inconsistencies don t let the queue have both p , q and q , p . </s>  <s> 2 remove an edge from the queue , and go to 1 . </s>  <s> if a marked edge is discovered to be inconsistent , then you lose . </s>  <s> if step 1 finds more than one face sharing a particular edge , then you lose . </s>  <s> otherwise , when done , all of the edges will be consistent . </s>  <s> which means that all of the surface normals will either point in or out . </s>  <s> deciding which way is out is left as an exercise ... kenneth sloan computer and information sciences university of alabama at birmingham 205 934 2213 115a campbell hall , uab station 205 934 5473 fax birmingham , al 35294 1170 </s>  <s> from steve lamont subject re finding fill me in on what 3do . </s>  <s> thanks , bh </s>  <s> from david watson subject re sphere from 4 points ? </s>  <s> in article , edward bolson writes given 4 points non coplanar , how does one find the sphere , that is , center and radius , exactly fitting those points ? </s>  <s> finding the circumcenter of a tetrahedron is discussed on page 33 in contouring a guide to the analysis and display of spatial data , by dave watson , pergamon press , 1992 , isbn 0 08 040286 0 , 321p . </s>  <s> each pair of tetrahedral vertices define a plane which is a perpendicular bisector of the line between that pair . </s>  <s> express each plane in the form ax by cz d and solve the set of simultaneous equations from any three of those planes that have a vertex in common all vertices are used . </s>  <s> the solution is the circumcenter . </s>  <s> dave watson internet department of mathematics the university of western australia tel 61 9 380 3359 nedlands , wa 6009 australia . </s>  <s> fax 61 9 380 1028 </s>  <s> from steve cunningham subject re siggraph scott r . </s>  <s> nelson writes dave mikelson writes ... does anyone know if there is an open day for the public at any time ? </s>  <s> </s>  <s> from henrik harmsen subject re 16 million vs 65 thousand colors andre t . </s>  <s> yew writes henrik harmsen writes 1 4 bits per r g b gives horrible machbanding visible in almost any picture . </s>  <s> 5 bits per r g b 32768 , 65000 colors gives visible machbanding color gradient picture has almost no machbanding . </s>  <s> this color resolution is see some small machbanding on the smooth color gradient picture , but all in all , there are situiations where you get visible mach banding even in a 24 bit card . </s>  <s> if you create a very smooth color gradient of dark green white yellow or something and turn up the contrast on the monitor , you will probably see some mach banding . </s>  <s> while I don t mean to damn henrik s attempt to be helpful here , he s using a common misconception that should be corrected . </s>  <s> mach banding will occur for any image . </s>  <s> it is not the color quantization you see when you don t have enough bits . </s>  <s> it is the human eye s response to transitions or edges between intensities . </s>  <s> the result is that colors near the transistion look brighter on the brighter side and darker on the darker side . </s>  <s> andre yeah , of course ... the term mach banding was not the correct one , it should ve been color quantization effect . </s>  <s> although a bad color quantization effect could result in some visible mach bands on a picture that was smooth before it was quantizised . </s>  <s> henrik harmsen internet chalmers university of technology , sweden . </s>  <s> I haven t lost my mind it s backed up on tape somewhere . </s>  <s> from s . </s>  <s> raj chaudhury subject re needed plotting package that does ... in chris murphy writes in article , glen fullmer writes looking for a graphics cad or
